16:50:02","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:02","title":"The (Literally) Unbelievable Story of the Original Fake News Network","link":"https://narratively.com/?p=79824","description":"<div style=\"margin: 5px 5% 10px 5%;\"><img src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/SetUp_HEADER_2580-1-scaled.jpg\" width=\"2048\" height=\"827\" title=\"\" alt=\"\" /></div><div><h4 id='pressboard-ad-sponsorship-tag' style='margin-bottom: 35px;'></h4><img width=\"640\" height=\"258\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/SetUp_HEADER_2580-1-640x258.jpg\" class=\"attachment-thumbnail size-thumbnail wp-post-image\" alt=\"\" style=\"clear:both; margin:0 0 1em 0;\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/SetUp_HEADER_2580-1-640x258.jpg 640w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/SetUp_HEADER_2580-1-1320x533.jpg 1320w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/SetUp_HEADER_2580-1-1600x646.jpg 1600w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/SetUp_HEADER_2580-1-1536x620.jpg 1536w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/SetUp_HEADER_2580-1-scaled.jpg 2048w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/SetUp_HEADER_2580-1-1290x521.jpg 1290w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 640px) 100vw, 640px\" /> <i>[]</i> <p><span class=\"dropcap\">G</span>uatemala City looked like a ghost town.</p>\n<p>The capital’s 450,000 residents hid in panicked self-quarantine, waiting for the first wave to arrive. World War I–style military planes periodically flew overhead, firing warning shots and dropping leaflets telling people to either flee or stay indoors.</p>\n<p>A civil war was moving toward them.</p>\n<p>All week, Guatemalan radio had been blasting the news of gruesome battles around the country. The newspapers were going crazy. Two Americans in a tourist plane had been shot down by Guatemala’s Communist army. Refugees were fleeing to Mexico while 400 injured Communist troops were retreating to the capital for medical treatment.</p>\n<p>Now, on Saturday morning — June 26, 1954 — radio news broadcasts reported that two columns of anti-Communist patriots calling themselves the “Liberation Army” were 60 kilometers from the capital. And marching fast.</p>\n<p>All vehicles were now military targets, the radio warned, so citizens should stay out of their cars. Trains had been stopped due to the intense air battle raging in the northeast. And a sabotage unit of the Liberation Army had just received orders to blow up a bridge in “Sector H-21.”</p>\n<p>Soldiers from the Communist government’s own military were now defecting in droves, newscasters reported. Five hundred and thirty-eight civilians had joined the Liberation Army just yesterday.</p>\n<p>In response, the government had suspended the constitution. The president had ordered all anti-Communists found on the streets to be rounded up.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_79864\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-79864\" style=\"width: 284px\" class=\"wp-caption alignleft\"><img class=\"wp-image-79864\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-01-scaled.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"284\" height=\"400\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-01-scaled.jpg 1454w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-01-937x1320.jpg 937w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-01-1136x1600.jpg 1136w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-01-454x640.jpg 454w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-01-1091x1536.jpg 1091w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 284px) 100vw, 284px\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-79864\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Colonel Jacobo Árbenz Guzmán, Guatemala’s second democratically elected President. (Photo courtesy Wikimedia)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The whole world was watching this catastrophe unfold, the radiomen reported.</p>\n<p>At 11 p.m., the broadcasters read aloud a message issued by the Guatemalan chief of police:</p>\n<p><em>To all Department Governors in the Republic. Capture immediately all mayors and other anti-Communist city officials currently affiliated with parties of the revolution. … Keep them in prison, and at the first shot fired when you are attacked, shoot them immediately.</em></p>\n<p>All weekend long, the radio newscasters implored government soldiers to stand down. Remaining at one’s post would only result in needless bloodshed, the newscasters warned. The only way to end the carnage was to abandon the president, who “preferred suicide to surrender.”</p>\n<p>Guatemala’s 41-year-old president, Colonel Jacobo Árbenz Guzmán, was not known for his sense of humor. But if there was anything that had the chance of making him smile that day, it might have been this last claim. Anyone who knew Jacobo Árbenz knew he would never say something like that.</p>\n<p>But he was not laughing, because what he knew was more infuriating than humorous.</p>\n<p>There was, in fact, no real “Liberation Army.” Just a few dozen pissed-off exiles hiding out 6 miles in from the border of Honduras, staging strategic photos for the press, like a bunch of 1950s-era Instagram influencers holding donated rifles. The “invasion” was more smoke than bombs.</p>\n<p>No refugees or injured soldiers had fled anywhere. The chief of police had not issued orders to round up anti-Communists. The two Americans in that “tourist” plane were actually the ones dropping leaflets, contract pilots. They hadn’t been shot down; they’d run out of gas and been captured by authorities in Mexico.</p>\n<p>There was no civil war about to engulf the capital, and most ironic of all: Guatemala was not a Communist state. President Árbenz was a political independent, having run as a moderate — and certainly was not a Communist. And though the country did have a small Communist Party and four representatives in Guatemala’s 56-member congress, not one Communist held a cabinet position in Árbenz’s administration. The president considered himself friends with two Communist Party leaders, but he was also friends with right-wing leaders. His own chief of armed forces and handpicked presidential successor was a conservative. Árbenz was a cool-headed military man like his counterpart President Eisenhower. True, in his ideal world, Árbenz would have Guatemala look like the USA under FDR. But he was a pragmatist. In the United States today, his policies would have been closer to those of Bill Clinton than Bernie Sanders.</p>\n<p>And that radio station everyone was reacting to? It wasn’t even in Guatemala. The disc jockeys aired their “reports” from a shack in Nicaragua. Many of their broadcasts had actually been prerecorded earlier in the year.</p>\n<p>In Florida.</p>\n<p>In an office belonging to the Central Intelligence Agency.</p>\n<p>The radio station that had all of Guatemala in such a frenzy was part of a secret CIA “<a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/setup#1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">terror program based on Orson Welles</a>,” <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">declassified documents now show</a>. It was overseen by an American actor and spy novelist whose salary was paid by U.S. tax dollars. The whole operation was, to use today’s parlance, “fake news.”</p>\n<div class=\"npagebreak\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/themes/narratively-wp-theme/images/pagebreak.svg\" /></div>\n<p><span class=\"dropcap\">B</span>y the following evening, President Árbenz’s colonels were refusing to leave their barracks. The president’s ambassador brought him word that the U.S. would end the charade if Árbenz stepped down. The radio, meanwhile, told civilians that all they needed for the war to be over was to stop supporting Árbenz.</p>\n<p>So they did. The Guatemalan people and military who had once overwhelmingly backed their elected president, Jacobo Árbenz, gave up their power. And now he had to.</p>\n<p>President Árbenz walked across the street into the Mexican Embassy, and the U.S. walked their man into his office.</p>\n<p>Árbenz was eventually strip-searched by U.S. agents and put on a plane, never to set foot in his home country again.</p>\n<div class=\"npagebreak\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/themes/narratively-wp-theme/images/pagebreak.svg\" /></div>\n<p><span class=\"dropcap\">U</span>nder Árbenz and his predecessor, President Juan Arevalo, the newly democratic Guatemala had been rapidly becoming a bright spot of stability and middle-class prosperity in Latin America. But the fall of Árbenz and subsequent collapse of democracy ushered in a string of brutal dictators who slaughtered countless innocents. It reversed Guatemala’s promising economic rise and led to the takeover of organized crime and mass immigration to Mexico and the United States.</p>\n<p>What if the U.S. had not intervened in Guatemala’s democratic process? When we posed this question to Martín Pellecer, founder of the investigative journalism outfit Nómada, in an interview in Guatemala City, he replied without hesitating: “We would have been Costa Rica.” In a series of reforms beginning a few years after Guatemala’s democratic revolution, Costa Rica abolished its army and redirected funds into a robust civil police force, infrastructure, health care and education — creating decades of peace, an enormous tourist draw and a booming economy for the region.</p>\n<p>Instead, the overthrowing of Árbenz — which CIA Director Allen Dulles and his deputies <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/setup/#doc2\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">in a secret telegram</a> immediately called “a great victory” and “an inspiration and a challenge to all of us” — closed the book on Guatemala’s 10 years of democracy and kicked off a civil war in which hundreds of thousands of innocent people died.</p>\n<p>Sylvia Brindis — one of the authors of this story — was born in Guatemala City during that war. Her family were campesinos (country folk) and coffee plantation workers from the eastern city of Zacapa. To this day her relatives regularly lament the fall of Árbenz. She grew up with a constant stream of “what ifs”: <em>What if the people had known the Liberation Army was fake? What if Árbenz had come back and staged a revolution instead of staying in exile? What if the democratic reforms hadn’t been undermined and reversed? </em></p>\n<p>The other author of this story, Shane Snow, has spent much of his journalistic career focused on human behavior and how media affects it. In 2014, he wrote a book chapter about Che Guevara’s use of pirate radio to help win the Cuban Revolution. When Sylvia learned about this, her immediate reaction was, “Oh yeah, like the CIA did in Guatemala.”</p>\n<p>Shane was surprised to hear this. Most in Guatemala know that media manipulation brought down their most popular president and changed the course of their nation’s history. But until 2016, most Americans had barely ever even heard of “fake news.”</p>\n<p>Our conversation about Che’s radio station led us to take a deep look at the Guatemalan radio story. In the mid-2000s, the U.S. government declassified a trove of secret documents about the overthrow. Unfortunately <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/setup/#doc10\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">the CIA told us </a><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/setup/#doc10\">that </a><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/setup/#doc10\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">they did not have any of the tapes </a><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/setup/#doc10\">that</a><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/setup/#doc10\"> broadcast Radio Liberación</a>. And the former CIA historian who wrote the agency’s “official” history on Árbenz told us that he’d never looked into the radio campaign because he thought it hadn’t been very important. This made us want to dig even more.</p>\n<p>So we spent a year poring through unorganized troves of declassified CIA and State Department documents, exploring Guatemalan police archives, and photographing boxes of correspondence. We interviewed historians who’d written books about various aspects of the saga, and tracked how key parts of their official histories were based on government misinformation. And we hunted down crumbly old Central American newspapers, half-written manuscripts left behind by deceased government agents, and documents the government claimed to have lost.</p>\n<p>And in that digging, we discovered something shocking.</p>\n<p>Not only did Che Guevara <em>get the idea</em> for his Cuban guerilla radio station from the CIA’s operation in Guatemala — the 26-year-old Argentine was on the ground in Guatemala City witnessing the overthrow — but our investigation also revealed a story about fake news that even the best Árbenz historians had never had primary access to, much less explored:</p>\n<p>In 1954, the CIA didn’t just use media manipulation to turn a country upside down and install the president that the U.S. wanted. The agency wrote <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/setup/#doc3\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><em>a six-stage, step-by-step playbook</em></a> for exactly how to do it.</p>\n<p>And the most unsettling part is this: It’s the same playbook that the Kremlin used in 2016 and is using against the United States again right now.</p>\n<p>Oh, and we also found The Tapes.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<h2><a href=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Setup-01.png\"><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-79849 aligncenter\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Setup-01-1320x78.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1320\" height=\"78\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Setup-01-1320x78.png 1320w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Setup-01-640x38.png 640w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Setup-01-1536x90.png 1536w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Setup-01-2048x120.png 2048w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1320px) 100vw, 1320px\" /></a></h2>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<div style=\"font-size: 10px; color: #cccccc; line-break: anywhere; word-break: normal; overflow: hidden; white-space: nowrap; text-overflow: ellipsis; font-family: Interstate,Lucida Grande,Lucida Sans Unicode,Lucida Sans,Garuda,Verdana,Tahoma,sans-serif; font-weight: 100;\">\n<p><iframe src=\"https://w.soundcloud.com/player/?url=https%3A//api.soundcloud.com/tracks/882316657&#38;color=%23ff5500&#38;auto_play=false&#38;hide_related=true&#38;show_comments=true&#38;show_user=true&#38;show_reposts=false&#38;show_teaser=false\" width=\"100%\" height=\"166\" frameborder=\"no\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></p>\n<div style=\"font-size: 10px; color: #cccccc; line-break: anywhere; word-break: normal; overflow: hidden; white-space: nowrap; text-overflow: ellipsis; font-family: Interstate,Lucida Grande,Lucida Sans Unicode,Lucida Sans,Garuda,Verdana,Tahoma,sans-serif; font-weight: 100;\">Actual audio of the maiden broadcast of Radio Liberación, May 1, 1954, created by the CIA. (Audio courtesy of National Archives and Records Administration)</div>\n</div>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><span class=\"dropcap\">T</span>he “revolution” had started two months earlier, on May 1, 1954, as Guatemalans amassed for their annual May Day parade, and a new radio station aired its maiden broadcast.</p>\n<p>The broadcast began with trumpet blasts and an orchestra rendition of the Guatemalan national anthem. Then, the voice of an experienced DJ announced (in Spanish):</p>\n<p>“This is Radio Liberación, operating from a secret location inside the Republic! … The soul of our people speaks through our mouth.”</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_79865\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-79865\" style=\"width: 317px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><a href=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-05-scaled.jpg\"><img class=\"wp-image-79865\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-05-1045x1320.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"317\" height=\"400\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-05-1045x1320.jpg 1045w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-05-1267x1600.jpg 1267w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-05-507x640.jpg 507w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-05-1216x1536.jpg 1216w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-05-scaled.jpg 1622w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 317px) 100vw, 317px\" /></a><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-79865\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Guatemalan First Lady María Cristina Vilanova Castro de Árbenz was known as the driving force behind her husband’s public career and political stances, often maneuvering behind the scenes on his behalf. (Photo courtesy Wikimedia)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The station declared that it was the news media arm of a coalition of exiles, university students, honorable military officers, and working Guatemalans who opposed their president. “We will announce the hour of your redemption,” the DJ declared, “[from] the presidency of the Communist traitor Jacobo Árbenz Guzmán!”</p>\n<p>He and a co-host explained that the radio broadcast would be airing twice a day with news of the rebellion against Árbenz. Each installment would begin with popular music and jokes, and then proceed to serious segments exposing the Árbenz government and the evils of Communism, which they said he had succumbed to. Several times, the DJs encouraged fellow “patriots” to join them and their leader, an exiled colonel named Carlos Castillo Armas, in their resistance movement.</p>\n<p>The broadcast ended with one of the many catchphrases that the station would soon repeat countless times: “The symbols of our fight: God, Fatherland and Liberty. And our aspirations: Truth, Justice and Work.”</p>\n<p>President Árbenz and his advisers — the closest of which were his politically savvy wife, María Vilanova, and his loyal foreign affairs minister, Guillermo Toriello — were surely frustrated to hear this. Castillo Armas had already tried to foment one of several failed coups in Guatemala’s short democratic history. He’d been caught and jailed in 1949 after trying to violently overthrow Árbenz’s predecessor, but he had since escaped into exile. Árbenz’s intelligence apparatus had documents proving that the rebel group had only a handful of men and a shoestring budget. They knew Castillo Armas was hiding in Honduras — not inside Guatemala — and was operating with support from a U.S. corporation known as the United Fruit Company.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_79866\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-79866\" style=\"width: 1000px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-06-scaled.jpg\"><img class=\"wp-image-79866\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-06-1320x844.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1000\" height=\"639\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-06-1320x844.jpg 1320w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-06-1600x1023.jpg 1600w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-06-640x409.jpg 640w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-06-1536x982.jpg 1536w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-06-scaled.jpg 2048w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" /></a><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-79866\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Foreign Affairs Minister Guillermo Toriello. (Image courtesy the authors)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>What could this radio station be up to, the Guatemalan president and his advisers wondered. Halfway through his six-year term, Árbenz remained overwhelmingly popular with the Guatemalan people. As a colonel himself, he had the support of his military. He knew that Castillo Armas posed no real threat, had few supporters and supplies.</p>\n<p>But what he didn’t know is that by the time Radio Liberación launched, replacing Árbenz with Castillo Armas had become the CIA’s number one priority. Nor did Árbenz know that President Eisenhower had authorized his overthrow so long ago that the agency was already on Stage 3 of its plan by the time the mysterious radio station had aired the Guatemalan national anthem for the first time.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<h2><a href=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Setup-02.png\"><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-79851 aligncenter\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Setup-02-1320x66.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1320\" height=\"66\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Setup-02-1320x66.png 1320w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Setup-02-640x32.png 640w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Setup-02-1536x76.png 1536w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1320px) 100vw, 1320px\" /></a></h2>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><span class=\"dropcap\">T</span>he United States was not at war with Guatemala in 1954. But the Boston-based conglomerate known as the United Fruit Company was at war with President Árbenz.</p>\n<p>United Fruit (also known as UFCO) had been cheating on its taxes for years, lying to the Guatemalan government about the value of its banana plantations and the hundreds of thousands of acres of unused land the company was sitting on. Now that Árbenz had passed an agrarian reform bill (similar to those that had in decades past allowed countries like Ireland, Colombia and Canada to break agricultural monopolies and create more competition), Guatemala was buying back untilled land for the value that companies like UFCO had reported on its tax bill. UFCO was being forced to sleep in the bed they’d made, and they were pissed.</p>\n<p>If only someone could get rid of Árbenz.</p>\n<p>The most powerful pair of brothers in the United States, Secretary of State John Foster Dulles and CIA Director Allen Dulles, were not legally allowed to do that sort of thing. But they wanted to. Both were UFCO shareholders and advocates, having worked for the firm for many years. But in a time of peace, well, doing anything more aggressive than writing angry letters would be illegal.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_79867\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-79867\" style=\"width: 850px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-07-scaled.jpg\"><img class=\"wp-image-79867\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-07-1320x1087.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"850\" height=\"700\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-07-1320x1087.jpg 1320w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-07-1600x1317.jpg 1600w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-07-640x527.jpg 640w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-07-1536x1265.jpg 1536w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-07-scaled.jpg 2048w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 850px) 100vw, 850px\" /></a><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-79867\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">(L to R) Allen Dulles, Director of the Central Intelligence Agency, and his older brother, Secretary of State John Foster Dulles. Together they were highly influential figures in U.S. foreign interventionist policy. (AP Photo/Jacob Harris)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The U.S. was, however, at symbolic “war” with Communism. Eisenhower had won the U.S. presidency on a campaign promise to stop its spread. And the Dulles brothers were particularly eager to help him do that. They held a deep religious belief that Jesus Christ had called on them to use their influence to spread American business interests across the world, while simultaneously beating back the Soviets. For decades, the United States had thrown its weight around Latin America when it suited the U.S. financially — such as seizing Puerto Rico from Spain and secretly helping Panama secede from Colombia. And in 1953, the U.S. successfully overthrew the Shah of Iran after he tried to nationalize oil. The success of that operation confirmed for the Dulleses that Communist prevention and American business interests were indeed a winning combination.</p>\n<p>So, <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/setup#5\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">even though the U.S. State Department knew </a><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/setup#5\">that </a><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/setup/#doc5\">Jacobo </a><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/setup#5\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Árbenz</a><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/setup#5\"> was not a </a><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/setup#5\">C</a><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/setup#5\">ommunist</a>, the Dulles brothers <a href=\"http://snowmedia.com/liberation/backstory/dulles\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">decided it was God’s plan</a> to get rid of him.</p>\n<p>This is not, strictly speaking, a legal justification for overthrowing a democratically elected leader of a nation. So the Dulleses decided to do so without anyone knowing about it.</p>\n<p>According to declassified documents, Allen Dulles had as far back as July 1952 <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/setup#doc13\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">proposed</a> putting together a private “syndicate” to fund Árbenz’s ouster. But after over a year of plotting, he and his brother got the official green light from Eisenhower to use U.S. tax funds to make Árbenz go away. As the U.S. diplomat over Central American affairs <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/setup#doc14\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">later put it</a>, “There is 100 percent determination here, from the top down, to get rid of this stinker.”</p>\n<p>Excited, they put an org chart together, where, as Harvard history professor John Coatsworth wrote in 2005 in the new introduction to the book <em>Bitter Fruit</em>, a journalistic investigation of the overthrow that was published in 1982 and revealed a number of details before the U.S. declassified them, “every policymaking official involved in the decision to overthrow the Guatemalan government, except for President Eisenhower himself, had a family or business connection to UFCO.”</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_79868\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-79868\" style=\"width: 259px\" class=\"wp-caption alignleft\"><a href=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-09-scaled.jpg\"><img class=\"wp-image-79868\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-09-856x1320.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"259\" height=\"400\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-09-856x1320.jpg 856w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-09-1038x1600.jpg 1038w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-09-415x640.jpg 415w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-09-996x1536.jpg 996w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-09-scaled.jpg 1328w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 259px) 100vw, 259px\" /></a><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-79868\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Frank Wisner, Deputy Director of Plans and founding member of the Central Intelligence Agency. (Photo courtesy the Central Intelligence Agency)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The covert operation would be officially run by the CIA, but the State Department would provide its Central American ambassadors as spies and operatives, <a href=\"https://snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/setup/#doc-11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">and the U.S. Information Agency would also lend support</a>. The United Fruit Company would not “officially” be involved, but it would provide transport, communications equipment and PR services.</p>\n<p>And in an example of positive affirmation that would make Oprah proud — if she were a mobster — the scheme was dubbed, Operation Success. Allen Dulles told his lieutenants that the operation, also called PBSuccess (PB was CIA code for Guatemala), was the agency’s “number one priority.”</p>\n<p>Allen Dulles’s number two man, Deputy Director of Plans Frank Wisner, spelled out the objectives <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/setup/#doc6\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">in a memorandum</a> on September 11, 1953:</p>\n<p>The operational overview officially included a $2.7 million budget breakdown, and falsely described the Guatemalan government as “Moscow influenced” and “thoroughly controlled by a Communist dominated bureaucracy.” It called the Central American nation “primitive,” with a “touchy, anti-foreign inferiority complex.”</p>\n<p>Thus the official record that U.S. agents would rely on in conducting the anti-Árbenz campaign was prepopulated with biased and false information.</p>\n<p>This was fitting, because, in addition to ceasing aid to Guatemala and pressuring its allies to abandon it, <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/setup#doc7\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">the central component of the plan revolved around fake news</a>. As Allen Dulles would spell out to Eisenhower: “The entire effort is thus more dependent upon psychological impact rather than actual military strength.”</p>\n<p>The Dulleses tapped the United States’ top “psychological warfare” experts to help CIA planners develop a six-stage playbook for making an information-centric overthrow happen. A secret document dated November 12, 1953, spelled this playbook out, step-by-step.</p>\n<p>What did this plan consist of?</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_79869\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-79869\" style=\"width: 1000px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-10-scaled.jpg\"><img class=\"wp-image-79869\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-10-1320x776.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1000\" height=\"587\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-10-1320x776.jpg 1320w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-10-1600x940.jpg 1600w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-10-640x376.jpg 640w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-10-1536x903.jpg 1536w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/00-setup-10-scaled.jpg 2048w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" /></a><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-79869\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Snippet of the detailed memo outlining the program for Operation PBSuccess. The CIA outlines their objectives, their statement of the problem, and the six-stage playbook of the operation.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>“It is difficult to explain without the wall map and charts,” Deputy Director Wisner explained <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/setup#doc8\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">in a coordination meeting</a> between CIA and State Department planners in the spring of 1954.</p>\n<p>But, he said, it most certainly included, “ghost voicing, deception, mines, bazookas, and fire power.” Everything they needed for a fake war.</p>\n<h2><strong>Narratively is thrilled to present this epic 7-part true story about the original fake news network. Click &#8220;Up Next&#8221; below to keep reading.</strong></h2>\n<div id='pressboard-ad-sponsorship-msg'></div>\n</div><p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" /2020/08/00-setup-10-1320x776.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn9@2020_3/2020/09/05/08-50-04-637_d98308e657f78984.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599295802275},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:02","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:02","title":"How to Subvert a Democracy, Stage 3: Create Your Own News","link":"https://narratively.com/?p=79857","description":"<div style=\"margin: 5px 5% 10px 5%;\"><img src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage03_HEADER_2580-3-scaled.jpg\" width=\"2048\" height=\"827\" title=\"\" alt=\"\" /></div><div><h4 id='pressboard-ad-sponsorship-tag' style='margin-bottom: 35px;'></h4><img width=\"640\" height=\"258\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage03_HEADER_2580-3-640x258.jpg\" class=\"attachment-thumbnail size-thumbnail wp-post-image\" alt=\"\" style=\"clear:both; margin:0 0 1em 0;\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage03_HEADER_2580-3-640x258.jpg 640w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage03_HEADER_2580-3-1320x533.jpg 1320w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage03_HEADER_2580-3-1600x646.jpg 1600w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage03_HEADER_2580-3-1536x620.jpg 1536w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage03_HEADER_2580-3-scaled.jpg 2048w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage03_HEADER_2580-3-1290x521.jpg 1290w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 640px) 100vw, 640px\" /> <i>[]</i> <h2><strong>You&#8217;re reading our <a href=\"https://narratively.com/collection/the-literally-unbelievable-story-of-the-original-fake-news-channel/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">7-part true story about the original fake news network</a>. Need to catch up? <a href=\"https://narratively.com/the-literally-unbelievable-story-of-the-original-fake-news-network/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Click here to start at the beginning</a>. </strong></h2>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><img class=\"wp-image-79947 aligncenter\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage-3.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"98\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage-3.png 975w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage-3-640x89.png 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_79945\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-79945\" style=\"width: 700px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img class=\"wp-image-79945\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage-3-g.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"34\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage-3-g.png 975w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage-3-g-640x32.png 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-79945\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Stage 3 in the CIA’s step-by-step plan to overthrow the government of Guatemala.</figcaption></figure>\n<p><span class=\"dropcap\">D</span>avid Phillips and his<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> radio crew spent March and April in Florida writing and prerecording the initial broadcasts for Radio Liberación. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In his memoir, Phillips recalled the objective as being “to intimidate listeners” who were Árbenz sympathizers and to “influence the mass of neutral types” — what they described as a “soap-opera audience.”</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Initially, these broadcasts would need to establish credibility. Anything that the Árbenz government could point to in order to prove that the station was not inside Guatemala, for example, could foil the plot. The content would start with exaggerations of the truth, opinions that would be hard to falsify, and accusations that would be difficult to disprove: Castillo Armas was building an army; Árbenz was bad for Guatemala; Communists were taking over the government; etc. The goal was to start getting Guatemalans talking about Castillo Armas and the fight against Communism.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Only after this would they move on to what Phillips called “the big lie.”</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">According to E. Howard Hunt’s memoir </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Undercover</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, after several weeks of work, the Guatemalan radio operators threatened to strike due to their “forced celibacy.” So Hunt flew out their “girlfriends” (at least one of whom was actually a wife). Hunt’s descriptions of the Guatemalan crew were exaggerated and racist (Hunt’s son Saint John describes his father as a racist in his own memoir), but the ladies can be heard in many recordings of the broadcasts, including participating in a regular “Women Against Communism” segment hosted by “Silvia and Sandra.” Documents reveal that they were sisters: Sonia and Sara Orellana.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Finally, in late April, the crew flew to </span><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage3/#doc3-1a\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Nicaragua</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, with permission from the dictator Anastasio Somoza, to set up a radio transmitter in a shack in the jungle. The </span><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage1/#doc1-5c\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">location</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> would be a heavily guarded secret — and Nicaragua was deliberately chosen because Árbenz’s military knew that Castillo Armas was hiding across the border in Honduras and might therefore search for the radio station there.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">With an established network and seeds of doubt firmly planted, the plotters were ready to start spreading their own content — what Silverman describes as the next step in a successful info-war campaign: “Get your operation up and running to get your message out.”</span></p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<h2><img class=\"aligncenter wp-image-79862\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage03-01.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1000\" height=\"104\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage03-01.png 3005w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage03-01-1320x137.png 1320w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage03-01-1600x167.png 1600w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage03-01-640x67.png 640w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage03-01-1536x160.png 1536w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage03-01-2048x213.png 2048w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" /></h2>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span class=\"dropcap\">T</span>he Guatemalan press reported excitedly on the new station that began broadcasting on 3420 kHz on May 1, 1954. Radio Liberación was launched strategically on this day, which was a national holiday that many Guatemalans had off from work.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">From then on, each day Phillips and his crew broadcast from 7 a.m. to 8 a.m. and from 9 p.m. to 10 p.m. — before and after work hours. Each broadcast had music, catch phrases and talking points delivered poetically. In between the sermon-like speeches, the DJs, Mario and Pepe, sprinkled in chatter, jokes and personal talk. Often, these voices from “a secret location within the republic” took on the tone of a friend filling you in on something.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Between the rumor mill about Árbenz’s tilt toward Communism — and the fact that the Árbenz administration had reported in January that Castillo Armas was plotting against him — the Guatemalan </span><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage3/#doc3-3a\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">press</span></a> <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage3/#doc3-3b\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">didn’t seem</span></a> <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage3/#doc3-3c\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">to question</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> whether the broadcasts really were coming from a group of anti-Communist exiles. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Not that everyone believed all the hype from Radio Liberación’s speeches. The Guatemalan military was skeptical, having been filled in on how small Castillo Armas’s rebel group actually was.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Among the Guatemalan public, Radio Liberación was in the minority when it decried Árbenz, or even Communists. The president was popular, and it was well-known that the Communist Party was small. And besides, the Communists supported agrarian reform, which was incredibly popular with the poor majority of Guatemalans.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">But in the 1950s, many Guatemalans still remembered the shady dealings of their pre-democracy dictators — and the smear campaign against Árbenz had created room for doubt about Árbenz too. So whereas many citizens approached the blatant propaganda on Radio Liberación with skepticism, they afforded similar skepticism to the rebuttals that the Árbenz government broadcast over official airwaves.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">And with its heavy repetition, the radio’s assertions about Árbenz started sounding more and more plausible. “Familiarity and repetition,” says author Craig Silverman, “the more you hear something, over time the more you believe it’s true.”</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Whether people initially believe your information is beside the point, though, media data expert Kathleen Jamieson explains. “What you want to do is change the media agenda,” she told us. “You want to change the balance of messages.” </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The more mentions of what you, the media manipulator, want discussed, the more that independent media feels pressured to report on it. And the more important those topics appear to the public.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In 2016, when Hillary Clinton fell ill at a 9/11 memorial ceremony, the Russian state news outlets RT and Sputnik released a drumbeat of stories questioning Clinton’s health. Russia’s network of disguised social media accounts promoted the narrative — along with conspiratorial stories about Clinton’s use of email while she was secretary of state. And when bad news came out about Trump, Russian state and social media </span><a href=\"https://apnews.com/fc9ab2b0bbc34f11bc10714100318ae1/AP-Exclusive:-Russia-Twitter-trolls-deflected-Trump-bad-news\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">broadcast deflection</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, which were picked up by Trump proponents, then discussed by the legitimate press.</span></p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_79890\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-79890\" style=\"width: 277px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><img class=\"wp-image-79890\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/03-Stage03-03-scaled-e1598447707840.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"277\" height=\"400\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-79890\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">The front page of the newspaper Prensa Libre claimed that a radio station had been found on the border near Honduras, May 4, 1954. (Image courtesy the authors)</figcaption></figure>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In an authoritarian system where you see media structures controlled by those in power, it’s almost impossible to subvert the media agenda of those in power, Jamieson told us. But, she said, “in an open system you can get the inadvertent complicity of the existing media.”</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The more Radio Liberación broadcast, the more the </span><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage3/#doc3-5a\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Guatemalan newspapers</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> and rumor mills discussed what it had to say. </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Was Árbenz secretly in cahoots with the USSR? Were Guatemalan women really organizing against Communism? What was going to happen when the Liberation Army mobilized? </span></i></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Guatemala’s own civil liberties — the freedom of the press and freedom of speech that Árbenz had helped usher in with the democratic revolution — worked against it when the CIA began broadcasting lies. Broadcasting itself was legal. Communist newspapers were free to campaign for their causes, and anti-Árbenz detractors were free to talk shit about him on the radio. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">What was not legal, however, was for a foreign government to foment a revolution. Hiding behind the “free speech” of Radio Liberación was an international crime. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Frustrated, Árbenz dispatched the military to search the jungle and find the station.</span></p>\n<div class=\"npagebreak\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/themes/narratively-wp-theme/images/pagebreak.svg\" /></div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span class=\"dropcap\">P</span>hillips and Hunt claim that the whole of Guatemala eventually began tuning in to Radio Liberación with bated breath each night.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">As propaganda men, it’s hard to imagine that they weren’t being a little hyperbolic. But CIA documents and Guatemalan news reports make it clear that the military, news media and a large portion of the public indeed paid close attention to the broadcasts, and that people who didn’t catch them live kept up on the brewing “revolution” through front page newspaper headlines. </span></p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_79888\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-79888\" style=\"width: 408px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img class=\"wp-image-79888\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/03-Stage03-01-scaled-e1598447660327.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"408\" height=\"600\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-79888\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">A CIA diagram of the radio transmission operation. (Documents courtesy NARA)</figcaption></figure>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Some of Radio</span> <span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Liberación’s “news” was relatively small, which gave it the air of a broader devotion to serving Guatemalans, as opposed to simply smearing the government. The DJs held “man on the street” interviews at the May Day parade, getting opinions from (supposedly) regular Guatemalans on the news of the day. At one point, they reported that a woman had been insulted at the airport for carrying copies of </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">El Rebelde</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, an anti-Communist publication. The DJs dedicated quite a bit of air time to teaching listeners patriotic song lyrics (which would turn out to be the “marching songs” of the Liberation Army). And they played plenty of music, from cumbia hits to the Berlin Symphony Orchestra. On Day 2, after delivering a 10-point treatise on why people should say no to Communism, Radio Liberación</span> <span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">played “That’s Amore” by Dean Martin.</span></p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_79889\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-79889\" style=\"width: 562px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img class=\"wp-image-79889\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/03-Stage03-02-scaled-e1598447677634.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"562\" height=\"600\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-79889\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Guatemalan Labor Day parade, May 1, 1954. (Photo courtesy NARA)</figcaption></figure>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">As the station established itself, it began broadcasting bolder falsehoods: that Russia was happy because now it could send planes on bombing missions to Los Angeles and have them safely land in Guatemala if it wanted to; that the government was no longer paying public school teachers; that Árbenz was spending money on expensive furs and Cadillacs while donating to a Soviet atomic bomb fund; and even that Árbenz was doing exactly what the CIA was up to. “The government’s principal propaganda mechanisms,” Radio Liberación</span> <span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">explained two weeks into broadcasting, “have been flooding the country with their disgusting product &#8230; in which salaried agitators try to win people over.”</span></p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><iframe src=\"https://w.soundcloud.com/player/?url=https%3A//api.soundcloud.com/tracks/882317260&#38;color=%23ff5500&#38;auto_play=false&#38;hide_related=false&#38;show_comments=true&#38;show_user=true&#38;show_reposts=false&#38;show_teaser=true\" width=\"100%\" height=\"166\" frameborder=\"no\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></p>\n<div style=\"font-size: 10px; color: #cccccc; line-break: anywhere; word-break: normal; overflow: hidden; white-space: nowrap; text-overflow: ellipsis; font-family: Interstate,Lucida Grande,Lucida Sans Unicode,Lucida Sans,Garuda,Verdana,Tahoma,sans-serif; font-weight: 100;\">Post-mortems credit the radio broadcasts as key to the success of the U.S.’s psychological warfare campaign against Árbenz. Though the CIA destroyed its</div>\n<div style=\"font-size: 10px; color: #cccccc; line-break: anywhere; word-break: normal; overflow: hidden; white-space: nowrap; text-overflow: ellipsis; font-family: Interstate,Lucida Grande,Lucida Sans Unicode,Lucida Sans,Garuda,Verdana,Tahoma,sans-serif; font-weight: 100;\">records from the Florida station where broadcasts were planned, and claimed to not have recordings of the broadcast reels, a Freedom of Information</div>\n<div style=\"font-size: 10px; color: #cccccc; line-break: anywhere; word-break: normal; overflow: hidden; white-space: nowrap; text-overflow: ellipsis; font-family: Interstate,Lucida Grande,Lucida Sans Unicode,Lucida Sans,Garuda,Verdana,Tahoma,sans-serif; font-weight: 100;\">request sent by Time magazine reporter Stephen Schlesinger in the 1970s may have inadvertently led to the broadcast reels being preserved and shelved</div>\n<div style=\"font-size: 10px; color: #cccccc; line-break: anywhere; word-break: normal; overflow: hidden; white-space: nowrap; text-overflow: ellipsis; font-family: Interstate,Lucida Grande,Lucida Sans Unicode,Lucida Sans,Garuda,Verdana,Tahoma,sans-serif; font-weight: 100;\">away for decades. We found tape recordings of those reels in 2020. <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/behind-the-scenes\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">See here for more details.</a></div>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">But the most chilling event was the broadcast that aired three and a half weeks in, on May 24. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">About eight minutes into a typical Radio Liberación</span> <span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">show, listeners heard a commotion in the background. The DJ pressed on even as the banging sounds got louder and voices in the background shushed each other.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Then, suddenly, the DJ started panicking. He announced that the station was being attacked. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The broadcast cut off midway through a woman’s scream. </span></p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><iframe src=\"https://w.soundcloud.com/player/?url=https%3A//api.soundcloud.com/tracks/882317479&#38;color=%23ff5500&#38;auto_play=false&#38;hide_related=false&#38;show_comments=true&#38;show_user=true&#38;show_reposts=false&#38;show_teaser=true\" width=\"100%\" height=\"166\" frameborder=\"no\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></p>\n<div style=\"font-size: 10px; color: #cccccc; line-break: anywhere; word-break: normal; overflow: hidden; white-space: pretended to be attacked by government forces.</div>\n<div id='pressboard-ad-sponsorship-msg'></div>\n</div><p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" id='pressboard-ad-sponsorship-tag' style='margin-bottom: 35px;'></h4><img width=\"640\" height=\"258\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage02_HEADER_2580-640x258.jpg\"
