https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage02_HEADER_2580-1536x620.jpg 1536w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage02_HEADER_2580-scaled.jpg 2048w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage02_HEADER_2580-1290x521.jpg 1290w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 640px) 100vw, 640px\" /> <i>[]</i> <h2><strong>You&#8217;re reading our <a href=\"https://narratively.com/collection/the-literally-unbelievable-story-of-the-original-fake-news-channel/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">7-part true story about the original fake news network</a>. Need to catch up? <a href=\"https://narratively.com/the-literally-unbelievable-story-of-the-original-fake-news-network/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Click here to start at the beginning</a>. </strong></h2>\n<figure id=\"attachment_79943\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-79943\" style=\"width: 700px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img class=\"wp-image-79943\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage-2.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"154\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage-2.png 975w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage-2-640x141.png 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-79943\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Stage 2 in the CIA’s step-by-step plan to overthrow the government of Guatemala.</figcaption></figure>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter\" /></p>\n<p><span class=\"dropcap\">I</span>t was 1951, and the inimitable Edward Bernays was holding court at United Fruit’s New York headquarters. The energetic nephew of Sigmund Freud, Bernays sported three-piece suits, well-manicured wavy hair, and a precise mustache over an infectious smile. He was charming as usual as he addressed United Fruit President Sam “The Bananaman” Zemurray.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">Bernays was doing what he did best: helping people come to a conclusion as if it were their own idea.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">Widely regarded as the father of the public relations industry, Bernays had successfully made the case that all American corporations needed to hire a “counsel on public relations” — and that doing so was good for democracy.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_79840\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-79840\" style=\"width: 325px\" class=\"wp-caption alignleft\"><img class=\"wp-image-79840\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/02-Stage02-01-e1598372825438.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"325\" height=\"400\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-79840\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Portrait of Edward Bernays. (Photo from his book, &#8220;Propaganda&#8221;)</figcaption></figure>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">“The conscious and intelligent manipulation of the organized habits and opinions of the masses is an important element in democratic society,” Bernays had argued in his 1928 book, <i>Propaganda</i>. “It might be better to have … committees of wise men who would choose our rulers, dictate our conduct, private and public, and decide upon the best types of clothes for us to wear and the best kinds of food for us to eat,” Bernays noted. But since that wasn’t how democracy worked, society needed “to be organized by leadership and propaganda.”</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">And because democracy operates on the principle of freedom of choice, such manipulation should be done subtly, Bernays added. If you want a man to buy a piano, for example, don’t tell him to buy a piano. Rather, Bernays wrote, you should “implant the idea in the mind of the general public” that having a music room is now fashionable. Then the idea of buying a piano “will come to him as if it is his own idea.”</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">This was not just how Bernays had successfully convinced women to smoke, diet-conscious people to eat bacon for breakfast, and overweight people to stay at the Waldorf hotel — all of which he did. It was also the psychology that had helped Bernays convince the world’s largest fruit company to hire him as its PR agent.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">Since the 1940s, Bernays had frequently consulted with Zemurray, and also worked closely with the company’s publicity director Ed Whitman, who happened to be the husband of Eisenhower’s personal secretary, Ann Whitman.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">For years, Bernays had warned Zemurray that the gulf between rich and poor in Guatemala could lead to social instability and PR problems for the fruit company. Now Bernays was concerned that anti–United Fruit sentiment might come to a head. Ever since its democratic revolution, Guatemala’s presidents had allowed labor movements and Communist sympathizers to operate legally within its country, and that potentially meant that the government might force United Fruit to make costly changes, like raising wages. Or worse: sell back its unused land.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">However, Bernays said, “Guatemala might respond to pitiless publicity in this country.” By alerting Americans to Communist dangers in Central America (or in his words, “Middle America”), Bernays said, the U.S. government might be persuaded to “take steps to improve the situation.” Ideally, Guatemala would back down and start praising United Fruit for being a job creator instead of a foreign plunderer.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">Zemurray, an immigrant from present-day Moldova who’d pulled himself up by his bootstraps (with the occasional help of some hired gunmen), was known for his racism against the indigenous people who worked his plantations. He wasn’t convinced that “Indians” were smart enough to ever gain negotiating power over him. But after two years of arguments from Bernays asserting that extolling the virtues of bananas wasn’t the only thing that PR could do to help United Fruit’s bottom line — and especially when President Árbenz got serious about agrarian reform — Zemurray finally relented.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">Yes, he agreed, something should be done.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">Zemurray’s instinct was to call up his friends in the U.S. government and ask for some favors. In 1953, United Fruit donated $64,000, in coordination with the CIA, to some disgruntled right-wing Guatemalans who wanted to start a rebellion, but their uprising was quickly crushed. The movement gained no favor with the Guatemalan public, and the CIA barely kept its role hidden.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">It’s unclear what Bernays knew about the cash being given to the rebels, but when he pressed on Zemurray that the smoothest way to win favorable treatment for United Fruit in Guatemala would be to sow seeds of doubt about Árbenz’s loyalty to democracy — and let people come to their own conclusions — Zemurray listened.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">“If we understand the mechanism and motives of the group mind, is it not possible to control and regiment the masses according to our will without their knowing it?” Bernays had mused in <i>Propaganda</i>. “If you can influence the leaders, either with or without their conscious cooperation, you automatically influence the group which they sway.”</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">For example, Bernays suggested to Zemurray, Ed Whitman could take U.S. reporters on a tour of Guatemala and persuade them that what they were seeing was Communism-in-embryo. Bernays could then call up his friends at <i>Time </i>magazine and <i>The New York Times</i> and persuade them to write a series on the growing influence of Communism in Latin America, based on those reports. He knew how deeply John Foster Dulles and Eisenhower opposed Communism, so he could make sure that those articles got into the hands of influential politicians. Those politicians would denounce Guatemala, and Bernays could get the press to write about that too. <a href=\"https://genius.com/397382\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">All of which</a> would make it easier for Eisenhower to intervene.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">Zemurray said to make it happen. And so, the Father of PR started making calls.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">Bernays organized a free trip to Guatemala for dozens of U.S. reporters, persuaded papers and magazines to extrapolate from his hints that Guatemala had Communist leanings, and got those reports in the hands of politicians, whose speeches were then quoted in more news reports. (What Bernays may not have known is how the CIA would end up facilitating the push of these misleading talking points within the U.S. political world.)</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">Sam Zemurray was no softie. Tall and well-built, with an Eastern European accent, he had “iron nerves and a powerful personality,” as Bernays wrote in a memoir. Zemurray had built a global conglomerate through ruthless action. For instance, when a deal to import equipment tax-free into Honduras in the 1920s fell apart, he paid Honduran exiles to overthrow the president — and got his business deal.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">As such, Zemurray thought that a little more would be needed than Bernays’s soft approach. So behind the PR man’s back, Zemurray also hired a former special forces soldier named John Clements to run an under-the-radar information operation targeting conservatives and hawks.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">United Fruit paid Clements and his associates to write a 235-page document called <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><i>Report on Guatemala</i></a><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-1\"> 1952</a>, that began with this sentence:</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter wp-image-79951\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Moscow.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"116\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Moscow.png 975w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Moscow-640x106.png 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">According to a contract soldier named <a href=\"https://spartacus-educational.com/JFKjohnsonRE.htm\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Robert Emmett Johnson</a> who decades later <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-22\">bragged in </a><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-22\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><i>Soldier of Fortune</i></a> <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-22\">m</a><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-22\">agazine</a> about Clements’s role in both dispatching information (and mercenaries) for Operation PBSuccess, UFCO paid the equivalent of around $340,000 in today’s money for the report.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">Zemurray also <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-2\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">hired well-connected lobbyists</a> to further push the narratives about Communism afoot in Guatemala.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">In all, United Fruit would spend half a million dollars a year on the campaign. And by the time the CIA got to Stage 2 of Operation Success, the agency couldn’t have been more happy about it.</p>\n<div class=\"npagebreak\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/themes/narratively-wp-theme/images/pagebreak.svg\" /></div>\n<p class=\"Normal1\"><span class=\"dropcap\">B</span>efore a population can truly fall for fake news about its government, one must, as the CIA put it in its description of Stage 2, “discredit target at home and abroad.”</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">It would do little good for Eisenhower to up and talk shit about his tiny neighbor’s popular democratic government. But if <i>Time</i> magazine were making innuendos — or the <i>Christian Science Monitor</i> or <i>The New York Times</i> were sounding a drumbeat of troubling assertions — the message that Árbenz’s Guatemala was not to be trusted would start to sound more and more plausible to the public. Even better if U.S. politicians could then reference those innuendos in official speeches, which could then be referenced <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-3b\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">in other news articles</a>, <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-4\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">further spreading the desired talking points while muddying their source</a>.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">It is at this stage that fake news expert Craig Silverman says one would want to “hire black PR firms” and “create lots of content.”</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">Today, <a href=\"https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1qoxtiT0gRrezrE97tayTN-RKT9pU13uRUwyS6fm80ac/edit#gid=0\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">billions of dollars</a> flow into the industry of “black PR.” In the Philippines, black PR is so in demand that regular PR firms feel pressured to offer it as a service, <a href=\"https://www.buzzfeednews.com/article/craigsilverman/disinformation-for-hire-black-pr-firms\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">according to BuzzFeed News</a>. In the mid-2000s the Pentagon paid the British PR firm Bell Pottinger $500 million to spread propaganda in Iraq, according to the <a href=\"http://labs.thebureauinvestigates.com/fake-news-and-false-flags/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Bureau of Investigative Journalism</a>.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">Silverman used the word “firms,” plural, for a reason. For a discrediting campaign to sink in, it should come from many angles. Bernays was a well-known liberal, ironically a bit of a bleeding heart. (Before the UFCO-Communism campaign, he’d pitched Zemurray on improving conditions for poor workers and getting rid of the company’s racist policies, like the rule that indigenous people must remove their hats when white people walked by — though he did point out that it was also a good PR move.) Hence, Zemurray was astute to hire multiple propagandists.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">It’s important to note that at this stage — true to Bernays’s stated principles of PR — the point was not to get people to <i>entirely</i> believe made-up information. Instead, the goal was to create an environment where people would be willing to doubt their previous notions and consider new ones.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">Similarly, much of the Russian disinformation campaign of 2016 — especially in the beginning — was not about convincing people of falsehoods. It was about sowing seeds of discredit and doubt about Hillary Clinton, and about the U.S. electoral system generally. It didn’t matter what was actually on Clinton’s email server, so long as talking about it cast doubt on her integrity.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">With PBSuccess, the campaign was particularly focused on amplifying doubt about Árbenz’s true political stance, exaggerating kernels of truth like Árbenz’s left-leaning politics, and giving more credence to existing fringe theories, like that the Soviet Union was grooming Guatemala to be its Communist outpost (of which there was no evidence).</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">The insinuations in American newspapers were deceptive enough that Guatemalan Ambassador Toriello complained to the U.S. State Department about them repeatedly. Getting nowhere, he eventually arranged to personally meet with John Foster Dulles to help set the record straight. He told Dulles that the articles depicting Árbenz and Guatemala as Communist were false.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">Dulles replied that “whether they were factual or not was beyond my knowledge.” But, <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-8\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">he lied</a>, he was “quite sure that they were not inspired for propaganda or malicious purposes.”</p>\n<div class=\"npagebreak\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/themes/narratively-wp-theme/images/pagebreak.svg\" /></div>\n<p class=\"Normal1\"><span class=\"dropcap\">B</span>ernays may not have known that his work would be wrapped into a secret CIA operation when he began the PR campaign to sow doubt about Jacobo Árbenz. But thanks to Bernays, by the time Eisenhower authorized Operation PBSuccess, those seeds of doubt were planted and ready for CIA watering.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">Yet, however grateful they were for United Fruit’s PR efforts, at Stage 2 the CIA needed to take control of the information narrative — and to step on the gas. So, as they ramped up for the launch of Radio Liberación, they began planting the Communism story into more official channels.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">“At a certain point, you want to get your information in more and more credible outlets,” Silverman explained. “If you can launder your stuff through established outlets, you can pull in politicians, NGOs, etc.”</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">This was exactly the plan. Though the CIA knew that Árbenz was neither a Communist himself nor owed the small group of Communists in his country anything, they treated the anti-Árbenz rumors circulating in the press as fact when briefing their operational teams, politicians and members of other government branches — including Eisenhower himself.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">The most egregious example of such “laundering” had to do with the <i>Report on Guatemala 1952</i> that United Fruit’s secretive PR firm John Clements &#38; Associates wrote<i>. </i>The CIA took the company’s name off the booklet and distributed it to members of Congress as their own report, according to one member of Clements’s team — perhaps the greatest feat of any pre–Red Bull corporate “content marketing” campaign ever. (Soon after, another John Clements booklet, the 96-page <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-10a\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><i>Report on Central America</i></a><i> </i>would become <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-10b\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">the basis for a grossly inaccurate National Security Council report</a>.)</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">With Árbenz discredited in the States, Operation PBSuccess turned to its network of moles to disseminate undermining stories about Árbenz within Guatemala — likewise starting with existing rumors, “to aim with increasing intensity and urgency at provoking first distrust and finally, open disaffection,” according to one State Department document.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter wp-image-79883\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage02-01.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1000\" height=\"110\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage02-01.png 2853w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage02-01-1320x145.png 1320w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage02-01-1600x176.png 1600w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage02-01-640x70.png 640w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage02-01-1536x169.png 1536w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage02-01-2048x225.png 2048w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" /></p>\n<h2 align=\"center\"></h2>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><span class=\"dropcap\">I</span>f the U.S. government had given out fun awards to its conspirators after Operation PBSuccess wrapped up, the award for “Most Eager to Participate” probably would have gone to U.S. Ambassador to Guatemala John Peurifoy.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">Big, loud and flashy, Peurifoy filled his bright-colored suits close to bursting, and wore snazzy ties. The trove of 2003 declassified documents are full of helpful suggestions from Peurifoy for everything from boycott ideas to whom might be most usefully assassinated.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_79841\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-79841\" style=\"width: 319px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><img class=\"wp-image-79841\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/02-Stage02-04-scaled-e1598372897165.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"319\" height=\"400\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-79841\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Sharp dresser John E. Peurifoy, U.S. ambassador to Guatemala. (Photo courtesy Library of Congress)</figcaption></figure>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">Secretary of State Dulles had thought that this ladder-climbing Democrat from South Carolina would serve as a good fall guy if the Republican State Department’s involvement were ever revealed. Ambassador Peurifoy was extra grateful for the appointment, and proved it.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">Soon after Peurifoy arrived in Guatemala, he and his wife had a rather tense dinner date with the Árbenzes. After dinner, Peurifoy cabled John Foster Dulles with a confident psychoanalysis of the Guatemalan president and the conclusion that the clock was ticking for the U.S. to get rid of him. A few days later, Peurifoy telegrammed Dulles with his own propaganda plan to step up pressure on Árbenz. Approved, Peurifoy began schmoozing with local reporters and working with the U.S. Information Agency to place Guatemala-Communism rumors in Latin American newspapers.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">Runner-up to Peurifoy’s “Most Eager” award may have been CIA agent E. Howard Hunt, the operative tasked with liaising between all of the members of the network inside Guatemala: the station chief; Colonel Castillo Armas; the rumor groups in Guatemala; the radio crew; and the Nicaraguan dictator Anastasio Somoza and his son Tachito, who were secretly supporting the rebels. Hunt relished in the spycraft and in meeting with new people — everyone was a potential character for his numerous sexy spy novels, with titles like <i>Be My Victim</i>.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">Hunt successfully established a flow of rumors from the CIA station to his moles around the country, as well as to Castillo Armas and other enemies of Árbenz.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">And with all this in place, the operation was ready to enter Stage 3.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_79842\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-79842\" style=\"width: 825px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img class=\"wp-image-79842\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/02-Stage02-05-and-06-e1598373113278.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"825\" height=\"600\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-79842\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Left, Nicaraguan dictator and Operation PBSuccess co-conspirator Anastasio Somoza. Right, son of Nicaraguan dictator and future Nicaraguan dictator, Anastasio &#8220;Tachito&#8221; Somoza Debayle. (Photos courtesy Wikimedia)</figcaption></figure>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">Everything was going as planned — until one of the members of the network suddenly double-crossed Hunt.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">It was a Panamanian attaché named Jorge Isaac Delgado who was helping liaise with the Nicaraguan dictator but was secretly in favor of President Árbenz.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">In late January of 1954, Delgado showed up in Guatemala City with a stack of stolen documents. The documents revealed the code names of some of the members of the CIA’s clandestine network, plus definitive proof that Nicaragua’s president was backing Castillo Armas in a coup attempt. And the documents included hints that the United States could be involved.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_79948\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-79948\" style=\"width: 700px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img class=\"wp-image-79948\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/02-Stage02-07-1-1320x321.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"170\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/02-Stage02-07-1-1320x321.png 1320w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/02-Stage02-07-1-1600x389.png 1600w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/02-Stage02-07-1-640x156.png 640w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/02-Stage02-07-1-1536x373.png 1536w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/02-Stage02-07-1-2048x498.png 2048w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-79948\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Some of the incriminating items included in documents known as The White Papers.</figcaption></figure>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">Previous historians had never been able to identify <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-12b\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">who Delgado stole these from</a>. But declassified documents now reveal that a CIA agent with the code name “Jacob R. Seekford” had gone to the hospital for ulcers and left the documents in his hotel room, where Delgado took them. Seekford tried to do damage control for a month, then was <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-13b\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">sent to D.C. in late February</a>, where he was told to lay low — perhaps take a vacation <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-13a\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">in Chicago</a>.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">By analyzing the evidence in State Department and CIA documents, we were able to determine that Seekford likely was E. Howard Hunt himself. Seekford’s job description was to be a <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-14a\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">liaison</a> between the Somozas in Nicaragua, Castillo Armas and the <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-14b\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">rumor agents</a> in Guatemala. <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-21\">Seekford was </a><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-21\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">compensated</a><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-21\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"> on the government pay scale of GS-12</a>, which meant he was a full-time U.S. employee at Hunt’s seniority level.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_79950\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-79950\" style=\"width: 700px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img class=\"wp-image-79950\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/02-Stage02-08-1-1320x429.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"228\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/02-Stage02-08-1-1320x429.png 1320w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/02-Stage02-08-1-1600x520.png 1600w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/02-Stage02-08-1-640x208.png 640w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/02-Stage02-08-1-1536x499.png 1536w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/02-Stage02-08-1-2048x666.png 2048w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/02-Stage02-08-1-1290x420.png 1290w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-79950\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">CIA memo detailing Seekford’s activities with Castillo Armas, codename CALLIGERIS.</figcaption></figure>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">In Hunt’s memoirs, he claimed that he had happened to be in Washington for the month of March 1954 by chance, so he’d been able to be there for his son Saint John’s birth. Hunt then said that Allen Dulles immediately sent him to Japan for another CIA assignment. “We need you badly in Tokyo,” Dulles had told him, Hunt claimed, 45 years later. “Please get on the next plane.”</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">But in an email interview, Saint John Hunt, <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B00A64PY1U/ref=dbs_a_def_rwt_bibl_vppi_i1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">author of two books about his parents’ careers as spies</a> (<a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B015VN46XW/ref=dbs_a_def_rwt_bibl_vppi_i2\">one of which has </a><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B015VN46XW/ref=dbs_a_def_rwt_bibl_vppi_i2\">a f</a><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B015VN46XW/ref=dbs_a_def_rwt_bibl_vppi_i2\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">oreword by Roger Stone</a>), said that the family did not move to Japan until six months after his birth in March — which checks out as a realistic time period for Seekford to have laid low. Further, the Hunts had family in Chicago, and E. Howard Hunt suffered from ulcers at the time. “As long as I [can] remember my father had ulcers,” Saint John Hunt told us.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">Hunt would later have his extramarital affairs monitored by the FBI, be repeatedly criticized in and out of the CIA for his sloppiness — <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-15\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">not the least of which included Watergate</a> — and riddle his memoirs with embellishments. It is not improbable that the propaganda man would lie about being reassigned out of such an important mission as if it were a promotion instead of a screw-up.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">Whether the document leak indeed came from Hunt, who died in 2007, or from a mystery agent with his same job description and stomach ulcers — what happened next proved that Stage 2 had been a complete success.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">The Árbenz administration <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-20b\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">gave the leaked documents to the press</a>, which <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-20a\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">reported</a> on the plot and the possible U.S. involvement. It was the biggest news story in Guatemala in some time.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">And the disclosure did &#8230; nothing.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">The world — and especially the U.S. — had already made its minds up about Árbenz and Guatemala.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">The few <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-16a\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">foreign outlets</a> that <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-16b\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">did report the news</a> declared that Árbenz’s evidence of the so-called plot was probably fake.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\"><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-17\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">CIA documents show</a> that the news articles calling Árbenz’s real news fake had a little help from Operation PBSuccess. The agency scrambled to get alternate facts into the hands of reporters — and also to get distracting fake stories into the news cycle within Guatemala in order to take people’s focus away from Árbenz’s disclosure of the plot. <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-18\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Distraction stories proposed by the CIA included</a><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-18\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"> flying saucer sightings and the birth of sextuplets.</a></p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">But because of Stage 2’s discrediting campaign, it wasn’t hard for reporters to believe the CIA’s lie that Árbenz’s revelation simply wasn’t true. And, of course, once Radio Liberación launched, it would repeat the lie over and over. “We reject Árbenz’s charges of a planned foreign invasion,” the DJs would announce on Day 2 of their broadcasts, before adding, “But there is indeed a conspiracy — a conspiracy of Christianity and civilization against Communism and barbarism.”</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\">By early March of 1954, State Department conspirators sat down for a meeting with CIA Deputy Director of Plans Frank Wisner to discuss the launch of Stage 3 — which would kick off the fake radio campaign, code-named “SHERWOOD” — and whether there would be a need to abandon the psychological warfare plan and just assassinate “15–20 Guatemalan leaders” and hope “for the Army to take over.” <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage2/#doc2-19\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">In the meeting</a>, they decided that the preconditioning had worked such that no matter what, the U.S. could keep its reputation clean as they moved forward.</p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\"><i>“What is the chance of U.S. exposure?”</i><i> </i></p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\"><i>“There is no official estimate yet &#8230; ”</i></p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\"><i>“After 1 April we will be too far committed to call off the operation.”</i><i> </i></p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\"><i>“Don’t worry”.</i><i> </i></p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\"><i>“Your job is to carry out instructions. You are to get the job done.”</i></p>\n<p class=\"Normal1\"><i>“Everything we do may be plausibly denied if uncovered.”</i></p>\n<div id='pressboard-ad-sponsorship-msg'></div>\n</div><p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://narratively.com/how-to-subvert-a-democracy-stage-2-condition-the-masses/\">How to Subvert a Democracy, Stage 2: Condition the Masses</a> appeared first on <a dn51@2020_3/2020/09/05/08-50-05-672_90bdef29b7d8f0e3.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599295802274},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:02","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 16:50:02","title":"How to Subvert a Democracy, Stage 1: Propaganda and Puppets","link":"https://narratively.com/?p=79827","description":"<div style=\"margin: 5px 5% 10px 5%;\"><img src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage01_HEADER_2580-scaled.jpg\" width=\"2048\" height=\"827\" title=\"\" alt=\"\" /></div><div><h4 id='pressboard-ad-sponsorship-tag' style='margin-bottom: 35px;'></h4><img width=\"640\" height=\"258\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage01_HEADER_2580-640x258.jpg\" class=\"attachment-thumbnail size-thumbnail wp-post-image\" alt=\"\" style=\"clear:both; margin:0 0 1em 0;\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage01_HEADER_2580-640x258.jpg 640w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage01_HEADER_2580-1320x533.jpg 1320w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage01_HEADER_2580-1600x646.jpg 1600w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage01_HEADER_2580-1536x620.jpg 1536w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage01_HEADER_2580-scaled.jpg 2048w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage01_HEADER_2580-1290x521.jpg 1290w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 640px) 100vw, 640px\" /> <i>[]</i> <h2><strong>You&#8217;re reading our <a href=\"https://narratively.com/collection/the-literally-unbelievable-story-of-the-original-fake-news-channel/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">7-part true story about the original fake news network</a>. Need to catch up? <a href=\"https://narratively.com/the-literally-unbelievable-story-of-the-original-fake-news-network/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Click here to start at the beginning</a>. </strong></h2>\n<figure id=\"attachment_79952\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-79952\" style=\"width: 700px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img class=\"wp-image-79952\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/stage-1.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"247\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/stage-1.png 975w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/stage-1-640x226.png 640w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-79952\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Stage 1 in the CIA&#8217;s step-by-step plan to overthrow the government of Guatemala.</figcaption></figure>\n<p><span class=\"dropcap\">T</span>he first order of business for any covert information operation is to staff up in a way that keeps the mastermind at maximum arm’s length from any dirty work. So once the Dulles brothers decided they were going to use psychological warfare to overthrow President Árbenz, they needed to figure out who exactly would do what — and how to keep the words “United States of America” out of it.</p>\n<p>This was relatively novel at the time — and also exciting. A brand-new agency called the Psychological Strategy Board was now part of the National Security Council, and the CIA under Dulles and Eisenhower was starting to flex muscles it hadn’t yet tried to use.</p>\n<p>At the CIA’s inception in 1947, President Truman had envisioned its job as collecting information, so that presidents could make better decisions. But, as Truman lamented years later <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage1/#doc1-1\">in a </a><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage1/#doc1-1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><em>Washington Post </em></a><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage1/#doc1-1\">op-ed</a>, the agency became an <em>operational</em> arm of government. “I had never thought that when I set up the CIA it would be injected into peacetime cloak and dagger operations,” Truman wrote.</p>\n<p>And yet, the year Truman left office, his successor, President Eisenhower, allowed the Dulles brothers to begin using the CIA to conduct paramilitary operations abroad while maintaining the nation’s PR-friendly image of law and order.</p>\n<p>During a time of peace, any aggressive action against another nation had to look like it came from someone <em>other</em> than the United States government. The cardinal principle of the CIA, therefore, became “<a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/setup/#doc3\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">plausible</a> <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage1/#doc1-2\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">deniability</a>.” This was of primary importance when staffing up PBSuccess:</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_79870\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-79870\" style=\"width: 1000px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-02.png\"><img class=\"wp-image-79870\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-02-1320x262.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1000\" height=\"198\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-02-1320x262.png 1320w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-02-1600x318.png 1600w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-02-640x127.png 640w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-02-1536x305.png 1536w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-02-2048x406.png 2048w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" /></a><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-79870\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">U.S. State Department officials discuss plausible deniability regarding Operation PBSuccess at a weekly meeting, according to an official memorandum.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The CIA planners agreed that the easiest way to overthrow Árbenz would be to convince the Guatemalan people to rise up against him. To do that, Operation PBSuccess would use what the CIA and the U.S. <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage1/#doc1-5a\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Psychological Strategy Board</a> called “black propaganda” — which it described helpfully in an internal document titled “<a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage1/#doc1-4\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Principles to Ensure Coordination of Gray Activities</a>” as content that is “partially or completely fabricated, but that which is fabricated is made to appear credible to the target audience.” (Propaganda during peacetime had been <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage1/#doc1-5b\">authorized by </a><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage1/#doc1-5b\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">the U.S. Security Council as a function of the State Department</a>, in order to keep it at arm’s length from President Eisenhower.)</p>\n<p>And in the event that the campaign didn’t convince Guatemalans to rise up themselves, black propaganda would provide a pretext for CIA operatives to pretend to <em>be</em> those Guatemalan rebels. But — since the U.S. was not at war with Guatemala, and helping depose a democratically elected leader would be both illegal and look supremely shitty — this would mean <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage1/#doc1-6a\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">staffing up</a> <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage1/#doc1-6b\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">with</a> <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage1/#doc1-6c\">outsiders</a> to abstract the CIA away from the dirty work.</p>\n<p>In a modern media manipulation campaign, fake news expert Craig Silverman, a respected media editor for BuzzFeed News and author of <a href=\"https://www.craigsilverman.ca/books\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><em>Lies, Damn Lies, and Viral Content</em></a>, calls this step “building out the network.” The social media equivalent of deploying businessmen and retired soldiers to mingle with and recruit Guatemalan locals as unwitting CIA minions is creating fake profiles on social networks.</p>\n<p>“What you want to think about is, how do you blend in and create the appearance that you’re an authentic actor?” Silverman explained in a phone interview when we asked him to break down the hypothetical stages of a successful modern fake news campaign — say, to overthrow the president of a small country.</p>\n<p>“You create your inauthentic network of accounts,” Silverman said, so that the propaganda messages appear to come from within the “target public’s” communities. This keeps them from getting suspicious. Even more authentic-looking, Silverman added, is to “buy some aged social media accounts” from real people who’ve been operating them for years.</p>\n<p>In Guatemala, this took the form of buying a preexisting enemy of the Árbenz regime to serve as the head of the supposed “rebel” movement.</p>\n<p>Thirty-six-year-old CIA field agent E. Howard Hunt — who would decades later go to prison for his role in masterminding the Watergate break-in — scouted several candidates, including former military leaders and a man who’d lost the election against Árbenz.</p>\n<p>Eventually, the agency settled on the perfect candidate, a legendary colonel named Carlos Castillo Armas.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_79873\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-79873\" style=\"width: 417px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img class=\"wp-image-79873\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-05-scaled.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"417\" height=\"500\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-05-scaled.jpg 1710w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-05-1102x1320.jpg 1102w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-05-1336x1600.jpg 1336w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-05-534x640.jpg 534w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-05-1282x1536.jpg 1282w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 417px) 100vw, 417px\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-79873\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">CIA field operative and spy novelist E. Howard Hunt, who would later be convicted of burglary, conspiracy and wiretapping for his involvement in the Watergate scandal. (Photo from his autobiography &#8220;American Spy&#8221;)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<h2><a href=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage01-01.png\"><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-79852 aligncenter\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage01-01-1320x88.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1320\" height=\"88\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage01-01-1320x88.png 1320w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage01-01-1600x107.png 1600w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage01-01-640x43.png 640w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage01-01-1536x103.png 1536w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage01-01-2048x137.png 2048w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1320px) 100vw, 1320px\" /></a></h2>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><em><span class=\"dropcap\">I</span>n 1949, Carlos Castillo Armas sat in his jail cell in Guatemala City, his well-toned chest and arm muscles visibly rippling from constant push-ups and chin-ups. Or so the prison guards thought. </em><em> </em></p>\n<p><em>Actually, for the entire month since his capture after attempting to take over a military barracks and overthrow Guatemalan President Juan José Arévalo, the mustachioed colonel had been hand-digging a secret tunnel underneath the prison. </em></p>\n<p><em>It would be back-breaking work for a regular man, but not for a killing machine like Castillo Armas.</em></p>\n<p><em>Finally, one night, after the prison guards had made their rounds, the colonel threw aside his mattress and wriggled his massive, muscular body through the tunnel and popped up outside the prison gates. By the time the sirens began shrieking, he’d sprinted so many kilometers that he barely heard them.</em></p>\n<p>Actually, that’s not what happened at all. But it’s what CIA planners told their agents.</p>\n<p>Castillo Armas was neither a beefy escape artist nor particularly intelligent. Rather, he was a scrawny, egotistical shit-talker. It appeared that he’d actually been bribed out of jail by friends and driven in a car to Honduras, where he’d been hiding ever since.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_79874\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-79874\" style=\"width: 971px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-06-scaled.jpg\"><img class=\"wp-image-79874\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-06-1320x951.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"971\" height=\"700\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-06-1320x951.jpg 1320w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-06-1600x1153.jpg 1600w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-06-640x461.jpg 640w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-06-1536x1107.jpg 1536w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-06-scaled.jpg 2048w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 971px) 100vw, 971px\" /></a><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-79874\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Col. Carlos Castillo Armas, with gun tucked into his belt, talking to his men during the Guatemalan Revolution. (Photo by George Silk/The LIFE Picture Collection via Getty Images)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The CIA settled on him among Hunt’s proposed options because <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage1/#doc1-8\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">they thought Castillo Armas would be easy to manipulate</a>. They paid him a <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage1/#doc1-7\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">$30,000 retainer</a>, gave him the CIA code name “RUFUS” and a pseudonym, “John H. Calligeris,” and promised him the Guatemalan presidency if he played the part.</p>\n<p>Thus the CIA bought the first authentic-looking part of its network.</p>\n<p>Hunt and his co-agents also <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage1/#doc1-9\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">hired local Guatemalans</a> as informants, graffiti artists and rumor-spreaders — though without disclosing that it was the U.S. government footing the bill. Eventually, the CIA even turned Guatemala’s small Communist Party’s number three activist, Carlos Manuel Pellecer, into a paid agent as well. Operating under the code name “LINLUCK,” Pellecer pretended to be Árbenz’s ally while filing secret reports on him.</p>\n<div class=\"npagebreak\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/themes/narratively-wp-theme/images/pagebreak.svg\" /></div>\n<p><span class=\"dropcap\">I</span>n the research for his 2019 book, <em>This Is Not Propaganda: Adventures in the War Against Reality</em>, British journalist Peter Pomerantsev discovered a Russian manual called <em>Information-Psychological War Operations: A Short Encyclopedia and Reference Guide</em>, which is described as a user’s guide for “state security services and civil servants.” The manual suggests that the deployment of information weapons “acts like an invisible radiation. … The population doesn’t even feel it is being acted upon. So the state doesn’t switch on its defense mechanisms.”</p>\n<p>The invisible radiation analogy is apt — and exactly what Stage 1 of the Guatemala playbook was about. It’s why, Pomerantsev explains in his book, Russia deploys social media surrogates to create and promote narratives that the Kremlin wants people to believe. If enough <em>people</em> are saying it, it doesn’t feel like the dictator is behind it. Running information warfare through a “network” that’s abstracted away from the mastermind is how Russia manipulated the American press and public in the 2016 election into talking about what Putin wanted — without them even knowing it. Research by scholars like University of Wisconsin professor Young Mie Kim <a href=\"https://journalism.wisc.edu/wp-content/blogs.dir/41/files/2018/09/Uncover.Kim_.v.5.0905181.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">reveals</a> that during the 2016 election, the Kremlin-backed Internet Research Agency created thousands of disguised social media accounts and over a hundred fake organizations and groups across Facebook, YouTube, Meetup, Twitter and independent websites, and ran thousands of ad and messaging campaigns from them — all of which was <a href=\"https://www.axios.com/russian-interference-2020-election-racial-injustice-7fa6a49b-03b4-4dc6-898d-fa589f9f0e6a.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">meant to look like it came from legitimate American nonprofits and groups of U.S. citizens</a>.</p>\n<p>“First, you would want to disguise your identity and your intent,” Dr. Kathleen Jamieson, a nonpartisan media data expert from UPenn, who rigorously calculated the impact of news manipulation during 2016, explained when we asked her what the first step in a modern disinformation campaign would likely be. “You would want to make it more difficult to pin the blame on you.”</p>\n<p>This is precisely what Special Counsel Robert Mueller found in his official investigation of 2016 — that the Kremlin used surrogates to build out its “network” for its interference campaign long before election season, both on social media and with in-person contacts.</p>\n<p>Rather than doing any dirty work directly, ideally, people within the Trump campaign could be influenced to take actions that Russia wanted. But Putin didn’t phone up candidate Trump. He had a friend of a friend of a friend schedule a meeting with Trump’s son — about “adoptions.” And the hackers who compromised the Clinton campaign’s emails weren’t Russian government either. The Special Counsel investigation found that they were a cyber-espionage group called Fancy Bear — in the <em>pay</em> of the Russian government. And the publisher of the embarrassing documents? Not Russia; not even the hackers. It was a party even further abstracted from Putin: Julian Assange of Wikileaks. Plausible deniability.</p>\n<p>And because of the way Wikileaks simply (and selectively) released the information, it wasn’t even Assange who told the American public the talking points Putin wanted Americans to hear. The final piece of the “network” was America’s own news media.</p>\n<p>“For practical purposes,” Dr. Jamieson told us, “the credibility of our major news outlets and some of our most respected reporters was used in service of Russian ends, inadvertently.”</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<h2><a href=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage01-02.png\"><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-79854 aligncenter\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage01-02-1320x71.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1320\" height=\"71\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage01-02-1320x71.png 1320w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage01-02-640x34.png 640w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage01-02-1536x82.png 1536w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Stage01-02-2048x110.png 2048w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1320px) 100vw, 1320px\" /></a></h2>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><span class=\"dropcap\">I</span>n early 1954, a Texan actor and playwright named David Atlee Phillips was working as an editor at a small newspaper in Chile, when the CIA called him up and offered him a new gig.</p>\n<p>A tall, charismatic man who fancied himself something of a spy-from-the-movies type (the first James Bond film had come out in 1953), Phillips had worked for the CIA in Chile for a few years, where his newspaper job gave him a plausible reason to talk to people the CIA wanted him to talk to. Based on his early CIA missions — and a stint in a Chilean movie in which Phillips <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage1/#doc1-14\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">described himself</a> as a “devil-may-care gringo who makes violent love to three passionate sisters one after another, uno, dos, tres” — he’d started trying to write sexy spy novels.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_79956\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-79956\" style=\"width: 346px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img class=\"wp-image-79956\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-07-1014x1320.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"346\" height=\"450\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-07-1014x1320.jpg 1014w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-07-1229x1600.jpg 1229w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-07-491x640.jpg 491w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-07-1179x1536.jpg 1179w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-07-scaled.jpg 1573w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 346px) 100vw, 346px\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-79956\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">David Atlee Phillips as a young soldier. (Courtesy the Library of Congress.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Now the agency wanted him to fly to Florida and make use of his writing skills for them.</p>\n<p>Operation PBSuccess had set up headquarters in Opa-Locka, Florida, about 14 miles northwest of Miami Beach. There, Phillips was briefed on the overthrow mission by CIA Assistant Deputy Director of Plans Tracy Barnes (whose name gets misspelled in the CIA’s official history as “Tracey”) and E. Howard Hunt, who’d helped recruit Castillo Armas and would be coordinating among the propaganda network.</p>\n<p>In his memoir, <em>The Night Watch</em>, Phillips claimed that Barnes told him, “Jacobo Árbenz is responding more and more to overtures from Moscow,” and “it’s unacceptable to have a Commie running Guatemala.” Already, Phillips was being compartmentalized from the truth.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_79875\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-79875\" style=\"width: 315px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><a href=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-07-scaled.gif\"><img class=\"wp-image-79875\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-07-1039x1320.gif\" alt=\"\" width=\"315\" height=\"400\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-07-1039x1320.gif 1039w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-07-1259x1600.gif 1259w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-07-504x640.gif 504w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-07-1209x1536.gif 1209w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-07-1611x2048.gif 1611w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 315px) 100vw, 315px\" /></a><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-79875\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Tracy Barnes, Central Intelligence Agency Assistant Deputy Director of Plans and Operation and PBSUCCESS conspirator. (Photo courtesy the Central Intelligence Agency)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>“I’m still not sure that gives us the right to intervene,” Phillips claimed he said.</p>\n<p>“Our marching orders on this operation come from President Eisenhower,” Barnes replied, according to Phillips. Barnes then told him the story about how Castillo Armas “tunneled out of prison,” which impressed Phillips. (The CIA knew <a href=\"https://sgndr.online/click?redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.snowmedia.com%2Fliberation%2Fdocuments%2Fstage1%2F%23doc1-10&#38;dID=1598441590947&#38;linkName=that%20the%20tunneling%20story%20was%20fiction\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://sgndr.online/click?redirect%3Dhttps%253A%252F%252Fwww.snowmedia.com%252Fliberation%252Fdocuments%252Fstage1%252F%2523doc1-10%26dID%3D1598441590947%26linkName%3Dthat%2520the%2520tunneling%2520story%2520was%2520fiction&#38;source=gmail&#38;ust=1598528377755000&#38;usg=AFQjCNGWlPdJrxQ63_8lPbkhccYO8qcriQ\">that the tunneling story was fiction</a>, yet briefed their agents with it anyway. Currently, <a href=\"https://sgndr.online/click?redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FCarlos_Castillo_Armas%23cite_note-FOOTNOTECullather199912-10&#38;dID=1598441590947&#38;linkName=the%20Wikipedia%20entry\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://sgndr.online/click?redirect%3Dhttps%253A%252F%252Fen.wikipedia.org%252Fwiki%252FCarlos_Castillo_Armas%2523cite_note-FOOTNOTECullather199912-10%26dID%3D1598441590947%26linkName%3Dthe%2520Wikipedia%2520entry&#38;source=gmail&#38;ust=1598528377755000&#38;usg=AFQjCNEOTdUvXQyNvedFrSG1nHBggHiI5A\">the Wikipedia entry</a> for Castillo Armas still mentions the tunnel story.)</p>\n<p>Barnes continued explaining that Castillo Armas was amassing an army — and the CIA’s job was simply “to assist the Guatemalans who are opposed to Árbenz.” It wasn’t a U.S. overthrow. It was assistance for a freedom fighter.</p>\n<p>Satisfied, Phillips agreed to oversee the writing for the propaganda radio station that would support the rebels. Barnes then left for Washington, and Phillips and Hunt drank rum cocktails and bonded over their shared love of writing spy novels.</p>\n<p>Phillips’s memoir is hardly a trustworthy source of information. Like his boss, Hunt, Phillips was a notorious self-promoter. (PBSuccess historians Stephen Schlesinger and Piero Gleijeses each interviewed Phillips before his death, and both told us that they remembered him as a self-aggrandizer who loved playing spy games — an impression that’s reinforced by <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage1/#doc1-13\">Phillips’</a><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage1/#doc1-13\">s</a><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage1/#doc1-13\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"> personal papers left behind after his death</a>.)</p>\n<p>Documents do confirm, though, that Phillips was indeed tasked with running Radio Liberación, after the CIA had <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage1/#doc1-10\">decided </a><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage1/#doc1-10\">that </a><a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage1/#doc1-10\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">it would be a bad idea to let Castillo Armas be in charge of it</a>. Phillips’s code name would be “<a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage1/#doc1-12\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">LANGEVIN</a>” — and he’d be <a href=\"https://www.snowmedia.com/liberation/documents/stage1/#doc1-12\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">managing</a> a team of Guatemalan exiles who the CIA had hired as the radio crew. The two head DJs were named Mario López Villatoro and Jose “Pepe” Toron Barrios. Another unnamed Guatemalan man would help them operate the station.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_79878\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-79878\" style=\"width: 413px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img class=\"wp-image-79878\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-08-new-1089x1320.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"413\" height=\"500\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-08-new-1089x1320.jpg 1089w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-08-new-1320x1600.jpg 1320w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-08-new-528x640.jpg 528w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-08-new-1267x1536.jpg 1267w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-08-new-scaled.jpg 1690w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 413px) 100vw, 413px\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-79878\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Mario López Villatoro and José “Pepe” Torón Barrios, the two head DJs for Radio Liberación. (Photo courtesy of The Center for Mesoamerican Research/Fototeca Guatemala at CIRMA)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>After a few drunken evenings at Miami nightclubs with his new team (according to Phillips), the actor arrived at headquarters in Opa-Locka to start his new job. At HQ, he saw just how sprawling the operation was: a diagram of all the players took up an entire wall of the office.</p>\n<p>We don’t have photos of the wall — Cullather told us that the CIA burned all of the documents housed at the Opa-Locka facility — but from the 2003 declassified documents, we’ve pieced together a map of the network that was on it.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_79877\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-79877\" style=\"width: 993px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-09.png\"><img class=\"wp-image-79877\" src=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-09-1320x931.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"993\" height=\"700\" srcset=\"https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-09-1320x931.png 1320w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-09-1600x1128.png 1600w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-09-640x451.png 640w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-09-1536x1083.png 1536w, https://narratively.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/01-Stage01-09-2048x1444.png 2048w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 993px) 100vw, 993px\" /></a><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-79877\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">A chart showing all the connections and conflicts of interests between U.S. government officials and the United Fruit Company that were uncovered by the authors while researching this story.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>With all this in place, the next stage, however, was not to jump straight to broadcasting fake news. First, some important seeds would need to be planted.</p>\n<div id='pressboard-ad-sponsorship-msg'></div>\n</div><p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\"
